<script>
    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

    <meta name="journal_id" content="41598"/>

    <meta name="dc.title" content="Chromosome-scale genome assembly for the duckweed Spirodela intermedia , integrating cytogenetic maps, PacBio and Oxford Nanopore libraries"/>

    <meta name="dc.source" content="Scientific Reports 2020 10:1"/>

    <meta name="dc.format" content="text/html"/>

    <meta name="dc.publisher" content="Nature Publishing Group"/>

    <meta name="dc.date" content="2020-11-05"/>

    <meta name="dc.type" content="OriginalPaper"/>

    <meta name="dc.language" content="En"/>

    <meta name="dc.copyright" content="2020 The Author(s)"/>

    <meta name="dc.rightsAgent" content="journalpermissions@springernature.com"/>

    <meta name="dc.description" content="Duckweeds are small, free-floating, morphologically highly reduced organisms belonging to the monocot order Alismatales. They display the most rapid growth among flowering plants, vary&#8201;~&#8201;14-fold in genome size and comprise five genera. Spirodela is the phylogenetically oldest genus with only two mainly asexually propagating species: S. polyrhiza (2n&#8201;=&#8201;40; 160 Mbp/1C) and S. intermedia (2n&#8201;=&#8201;36; 160 Mbp/1C). This study combined comparative cytogenetics and de novo genome assembly based on PacBio, Illumina and Oxford Nanopore (ON) reads to obtain the first genome reference for S. intermedia and to compare its genomic features with those of the sister species S. polyrhiza. Both species&#8217; genomes revealed little more than 20,000 putative protein-coding genes, very low rDNA copy numbers and a low amount of repetitive sequences, mainly Ty3/gypsy retroelements. The detection of a few new small chromosome rearrangements between both Spirodela species refined the karyotype and the chromosomal sequence assignment for S. intermedia."/>

    <meta name="description" content="Duckweeds are small, free-floating, morphologically highly reduced organisms belonging to the monocot order Alismatales. They display the most rapid growth among flowering plants, vary&#8201;~&#8201;14-fold in genome size and comprise five genera. Spirodela is the phylogenetically oldest genus with only two mainly asexually propagating species: S. polyrhiza (2n&#8201;=&#8201;40; 160 Mbp/1C) and S. intermedia (2n&#8201;=&#8201;36; 160 Mbp/1C). The detection of a few new small chromosome rearrangements between both Spirodela species refined the karyotype and the chromosomal sequence assignment for S. intermedia."/>

            <div class="c-article-body">
                <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Duckweeds are small, free-floating, morphologically highly reduced organisms belonging to the monocot order Alismatales. They display the most rapid growth among flowering plants, vary ~ 14-fold in genome size and comprise five genera. Spirodela is the phylogenetically oldest genus with only two mainly asexually propagating species: <i>S. polyrhiza</i> (2n = 40; 160 Mbp/1C) and <i>S. intermedia</i> (2n = 36; 160 Mbp/1C). This study combined comparative cytogenetics and de novo genome assembly based on PacBio, Illumina and Oxford Nanopore (ON) reads to obtain the first genome reference for <i>S. intermedia</i> and to compare its genomic features with those of the sister species <i>S. polyrhiza</i>. Both species’ genomes revealed little more than 20,000 putative protein-coding genes, very low rDNA copy numbers and a low amount of repetitive sequences, mainly Ty3/gypsy retroelements. The detection of a few new small chromosome rearrangements between both <i>Spirodela</i> species refined the karyotype and the chromosomal sequence assignment for <i>S. intermedia.</i></p></div></div></section>
                <noscript>
                    
                </noscript>

                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Duckweeds are the smallest and fastest-growing flowering plants, and are considered as potential aquatic crops, serving for feed, food, fuel and waste water remediation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Goswami, C., Majumder, A., Misra, A. K. &amp; Bandyopadhyay, K. Arsenic uptake by Lemna minor in hydroponic system. Int. J. Phytoremediation 16, 1221–1227. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/15226514.2013.821452&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Tatar, ŞY. &amp; Öbek, E. Potential of Lemna gibba L. and Lemna minor L. for accumulation of Boron from secondary effluents. Ecol. Eng. 70, 332–336. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ecoleng.2014.06.033&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Teixeira, S., Vieira, M. N., Espinha Marques, J. &amp; Pereira, R. Bioremediation of an iron-rich mine effluent by Lemna minor. Int. J. Phytoremediation 16, 1228–1240. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/15226514.2013.821454&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_2">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Verma, R. &amp; Suthar, S. Synchronized urban wastewater treatment and biomass production using duckweed Lemna gibba L. Ecol. Eng. 64, 337–343. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ecoleng.2013.12.055&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_3">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Fourounjian, P., Fakhoorian, T. &amp; Cao, X. Importance of duckweeds in basic research and their industrial applications. In The Duckweed Genomes (eds Cao, X. H. et al.) 1–17 (Springer, Berlin, 2020). &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-030-11045-1_1&#xA;                  &#xA;                ." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_4">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Vu, G., Fourounjian, P., Wang, W. &amp; Cao, X. Future prospects of duckweed research and applications. In The Duckweed Genomes (eds Cao, X. H. et al.) 179–185 (Springer, Berlin, 2020). &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-030-11045-1_18&#xA;                  &#xA;                ." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_5">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ziegler, P., Sree, K. S. &amp; Appenroth, K. J. Duckweeds for water remediation and toxicity testing. Toxicol. Environ. Chem. 98, 1127–1154. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1080/02772248.2015.1094701&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_6">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ziegler, P., Sree, K. S. &amp; Appenroth, K. J. The uses of duckweed in relation to water remediation. Desalination &amp; Water Treatment, 63, 327–342 (2017). In 5th International Conference on Environmental Management, Engineering, Planning and Economics, Vol. 63, 327–342 (Balaban Publishers - Desalination Publications, Mykonos, Greece, 2017)." href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_7">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ziegler, P., Adelmann, K., Zimmer, S., Schmidt, C. &amp; Appenroth, K. J. Relative in vitro growth rates of duckweeds (Lemnaceae)—the most rapidly growing higher plants. Plant Biol. 17(Suppl 1), 33–41. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/plb.12184&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_8">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Appenroth, K.-J. et al. Nutritional value of the duckweed species of the genus Wolffia (Lemnaceae) as human food. Front. Chem. 6, 483. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3389/fchem.2018.00483&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_9">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sońta, M., Rekiel, A. &amp; Batorska, M. Use of duckweed (Lemna L.) in sustainable livestock production and aquaculture: a review. Ann. Anim. Sci. 19, 257–271. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.2478/aoas-2018-0048&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_10">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren, H. et al. Enhanced biogas production in the duckweed anaerobic digestion process. J. Energy Resour. Technol. 140, 041805. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1115/1.4039782&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d46614e585_11">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Cui, W. &amp; Cheng, J. J. Growing duckweed for biofuel production: a review. Plant Biol. 17(Suppl 1), 16–23. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/plb.12216&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d46614e588">13</a></sup>. They comprise 36 largely asexually propagating species within the 5 genera Spirodela, Landoltia, Lemna, Wolffiella and Wolffia<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bog, M. et al. Genetic structure of the genus Lemna L. (Lemnaceae) as revealed by amplified fragment length polymorphism. Planta 232, 609–619. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00425-010-1201-2&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2010)." href="#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d46614e592">14</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bog, M. et al. A taxonomic revision of Lemna sect. Uninerves (Lemnaceae). Taxon 69, 56–66. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1002/tax.12188&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2020)." href="#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d46614e592_1">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Tippery, N. P., Les, D. H. &amp; Crawford, D. J. Evaluation of phylogenetic relationships in Lemnaceae using nuclear ribosomal data. Plant Biol. 17(Suppl 1), 50–58. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/plb.12203&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d46614e595">16</a></sup> With decreasing phylogenetic age duckweed frond sizes decrease from 1.5 cm to less than 1 mm in diameter accompanied by a successive reduction or loss of roots and a nearly 14-fold genome size variation (from 160 to 2203 Mbp)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bog, M. et al. Genetic characterization and barcoding of taxa in the genera Landoltia and Spirodela (Lemnaceae) by three plastidic markers and amplified fragment length polymorphism (AFLP). Hydrobiologia 749, 169–182. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s10750-014-2163-3&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d46614e599">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Hoang, P. T. N., Schubert, V., Meister, A., Fuchs, J. &amp; Schubert, I. Variation in genome size, cell and nucleus volume, chromosome number and rDNA loci among duckweeds. Sci. Rep. 9, 3234. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-019-39332-w&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d46614e599_1">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Landolt, E. The family of Lemnaceae: a monographic study (Vol 1) (Veröffentlichungen des Geobotanischen Institutes der Eidg. Techn. Hochschule, Zürich, 1986)." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d46614e599_2">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Wang, W., Kerstetter, R. A. &amp; Michael, T. P. Evolution of genome size in duckweeds (Lemnaceae). J. Bot. 1–9, 2011. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1155/2011/570319&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2011)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d46614e602">20</a></sup>. These features make duckweeds an interesting subject for genome and karyotype evolution studies. So far, no correlation between genome size, chromosome number as well as ribosomal DNA loci was recorded from eleven species representative for five duckweed genera<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Hoang, P. T. N., Schubert, V., Meister, A., Fuchs, J. &amp; Schubert, I. Variation in genome size, cell and nucleus volume, chromosome number and rDNA loci among duckweeds. Sci. Rep. 9, 3234. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-019-39332-w&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d46614e606">18</a></sup>.



</p><p>The genus Spirodela harbors only two species of similar genome size (160 Mbp), <i>S. polyrhiza</i> and S<i>. intermedia</i>. Due to its basal ancestral phylogenetic position, its industrial potential and its small genome, the Greater Duckweed <i>S. polyrhiza</i> was chosen as the first duckweed for whole genome sequencing<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Wang, W. et al. The Spirodela polyrhiza genome reveals insights into its neotenous reduction fast growth and aquatic lifestyle. Nat. Commun. 5, 3311. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/ncomms4311&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d46614e622">21</a></sup>. By integrating different approaches: cytogenetics, optical mapping (BioNano technique), Hi-C chromatin conformation study, 454, Illumina and Oxford Nanopore sequencing platforms, a high-confidence genome map for <i>S. polyrhiza</i> was established<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Harkess, A. et al. A new Spirodela polyrhiza genome and proteome reveal a conserved chromosomal structure with high abundances of proteins favoring energy production. J. bioRxiv &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1101/2020.01.23.909457&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2020)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d46614e630">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Hoang, P. N. T. et al. Generating a high-confidence reference genome map of the Greater Duckweed by integration of cytogenomic, optical mapping and Oxford Nanopore technologies. Plant J. 96, 670–684. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.14049&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d46614e633">24</a></sup> that corrected the errors of previous genome maps<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Wang, W. et al. The Spirodela polyrhiza genome reveals insights into its neotenous reduction fast growth and aquatic lifestyle. Nat. Commun. 5, 3311. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/ncomms4311&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d46614e637">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Cao, H. X. et al. The map-based genome sequence of Spirodela polyrhiza aligned with its chromosomes, a reference for karyotype evolution. New Phytol. 209, 354–363. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/nph.13592&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d46614e640">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Hoang, P. N. T. et al. Generating a high-confidence reference genome map of the Greater Duckweed by integration of cytogenomic, optical mapping and Oxford Nanopore technologies. Plant J. 96, 670–684. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.14049&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d46614e640_1">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Michael, T. P. et al. Comprehensive definition of genome features in Spirodela polyrhiza by high-depth physical mapping and short-read DNA sequencing strategies. Plant J. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.13400&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d46614e643">25</a></sup>. This high-quality genome map provides a source for advanced genomic research regarding repetitive sequences and protein-coding genes, their chromosomal location and evolutionary history in other duckweeds. Moreover, whole-genome duplication (WGD) events and chromosomal rearrangement between duckweed species can potentially be uncovered using the <i>S. polyrhiza</i> genome as a reference. Between the chromosomes of seven cytogenetically investigated <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clones so far no BAC-sized structural rearrangements were found<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Hoang, P. N. T. et al. Generating a high-confidence reference genome map of the Greater Duckweed by integration of cytogenomic, optical mapping and Oxford Nanopore technologies. Plant J. 96, 670–684. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.14049&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d46614e653">24</a></sup>. In addition, population genomics studies suggested a considerably low genetic diversity between world-wide distributed <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clones<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Ho, E. K. H., Bartkowska, M., Wright, S. I. &amp; Agrawal, A. F. Population genomics of the facultatively asexual duckweed Spirodela polyrhiza. New Phytol. 224, 1361–1371. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/nph.16056&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d46614e661">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Xu, S. et al. Low genetic variation is associated with low mutation rate in the giant duckweed. Nat. Commun. 10, 1243. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-019-09235-5&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d46614e664">27</a></sup>.</p><p>Sequence assignment to distinct chromosomes based on cross-hybridization of genomic sequences between related species represents a novel cytogenomic approach<i>.</i> Such an approach is particularly important for vegetatively propagating species<i>,</i> for which obtaining a genetic map to validate sequence assembly is difficult. However, in such cases at least one reference genome for validating bioinformatic assembly efforts is required, and a considerable number of cytogenetic anchor points should provide a reliable support for sequence data integration as previously exemplified for <i>Amborella trichopoda</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Chamala, S. et al. Assembly and validation of the genome of the nonmodel basal angiosperm Amborella. Science 342, 1516–1517. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1126/science.1241130&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d46614e679">28</a></sup> and for <i>S. polyrhiza</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Cao, H. X. et al. The map-based genome sequence of Spirodela polyrhiza aligned with its chromosomes, a reference for karyotype evolution. New Phytol. 209, 354–363. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/nph.13592&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d46614e685">23</a></sup>. These prerequisites are given for <i>S. intermedia.</i> In our previous study, chromosome homeology and rearrangements between <i>S. polyrhiza</i> (2n = 40) and <i>S. intermedia</i> (2n = 36) were investigated by cross-FISH with 93 anchor BACs of <i>S. polyrhiza</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e701">29</a></sup>. Thus, a high-confidence genome map of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> as a reference, and a cytogenetic map of <i>S. intermedia</i> are available to support genomic sequence assembly from reads generated by next-generation sequencing (NGS) platforms.</p><p>In this study, the cytogenetic maps of two <i>S. intermedia</i> clones (8410 and 7747) served as a frame for whole genome assembly of the vegetatively propagating <i>S. intermedia.</i> The same chromosomal rearrangements distinguishing clone 8410 from <i>S. polyrhiza</i> were also found for clone 7747 applying 93 anchored BACs. By integrating the cytogenetic maps and genome assembly from PacBio reads for clone 7747 and Illumina/ON reads for clone 8410, we generated a robust, chromosome-scaled genome map, apparently identical for both <i>S. intermedia</i> clones and revealed additionally further small evolutionary rearrangements between the two Spirodela species.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec2" data-title="Results"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Results</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">The cytogenetic map for <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747</h3><p>Previously we established a cytogenetic map for <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 8410 using 93 BACs anchored in the <i>S. polyrhiza</i> genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e749">29</a></sup>. Now we hybridized diagnostic BACs to the chromosomes of the <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747 in order to test whether chromosomal differences occurred between the karyotypes of these two <i>S. intermedia</i> clones, because different chromosome numbers (2n = 36 versus 2n = 20) have been reported for <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Geber, G. Zur Karyosystematik der Lemnaceae. Ph.D. thesis, University of Vienna, Vienna, Austria, p.140 (1989)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d46614e763">30</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title='Urbanska-Worytkiewicz, K. Cytological variation within the family of &#34;Lemnaceae&#34;. Veröffentlichungen des Geobotanischen Institutes der Eidg. Tech. Hochschule, Stiftung Rübel, in Zürich. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.5169/seals-308615&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (1980).' href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d46614e766">31</a></sup>. Our current chromosome counting found no chromosome number difference between clones 7747 and 8410. For both clones 2n = 36 were counted<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Hoang, P. T. N., Schubert, V., Meister, A., Fuchs, J. &amp; Schubert, I. Variation in genome size, cell and nucleus volume, chromosome number and rDNA loci among duckweeds. Sci. Rep. 9, 3234. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-019-39332-w&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2019)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d46614e770">18</a></sup> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S1</a>). In order to test whether structural chromosomal rearrangements occurred between these <i>S. intermedia</i> clones, we applied cross-FISH with suitable combinations of 93 <i>S. polyrhiza</i> BACs, as described in Hoang &amp; Schubert, 2017<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e784">29</a></sup>, on mitotic spreads of <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747. We used the same chromosome designation as in Hoang &amp; Schubert, 2017<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e791">29</a></sup>: ChrSp for <u>chr</u>omosomes of <i><u>S. polyrhiza</u></i> and ChrSi for <u>chr</u>omosomes of <i><u>S. intermedia</u></i>. No chromosomal rearrangements between these two <i>S. intermedia</i> clones were detected. Six linkages in <i>S. intermedia</i> that differed from the <i>S. polyrhiza</i> karyotype [ChrSp03–ChrSp06–ChrSp14]; [ChrSp05–ChrSp06]; [ChrSp06–ChrSp07–ChrSp14]; [ChrSp03–ChrSp17], [ChrSp10–ChrSp16] and [ChrSp08–ChrSp18] previously reported for clone 8410<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e817">29</a></sup>, were found also for clone 7747 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig1">1</a>). The similarity between the cytogenetic maps of <i>S. intermedia</i> clones 7747 and 8410 enabled merging of genome assembly from PacBio reads for clone 7747 and of Illumina and ON reads for clone 8410, and yielded an apparently identical genome map for both <i>S. intermedia</i> clones<i>.</i></p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Figure 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig1_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-1-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig1_HTML.jpg" alt="figure1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="757" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>Six linkages due to chromosome rearrangements between <i>S. polyrhiza and S. intermedia</i> (clone 8410) are also present in the sequenced clone 7747. (<b>a</b>) ChrSp05–ChrSp06 = ChrSi06; (<b>b</b>) ChrSp08–ChrSp18 = ChrSi09; (<b>c</b>) ChrSp03–ChrSp17 = ChrSi04; (<b>d</b>) ChrSp10–ChrSp16 = ChrSi11; (<b>e</b>) ChrSp06–ChrSp07–ChrSp14 = ChrSi07; (<b>f</b>) ChrSp03–ChrSp06–ChrSp14 = ChrSi03. See also Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a>. Scale bars = 5 µm.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Genome assembly for <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747 based on the library of PacBio sequence reads</h3><p>Two rounds of PacBio-sequencing of a 20 kb library of genomic DNA of <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747 resulted in 149 Gbp of raw read data. After an initial filtering for potential bacterial contamination, reads of at least 500 nucleotides were assembled using the Canu pipeline v. 1.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Koren, S. et al. Canu: scalable and accurate long-read assembly via adaptive k-mer weighting and repeat separation. Genome Res. 27, 722–736. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1101/gr.215087.116&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d46614e891">32</a></sup>.</p><p>A total of 1,305,064 reads were assembled into 1172 sequence contigs of 147,613,042 nucleotides, corresponding 91.7% of the estimated genome size<i>.</i> All contigs of this draft assembly are covered in median 37.5-fold by raw reads. In a first round of scaffolding, the two genomes of the sister species <i>S. polyrhiza</i> (from clones 9505 and 7498)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Cao, H. X. et al. The map-based genome sequence of Spirodela polyrhiza aligned with its chromosomes, a reference for karyotype evolution. New Phytol. 209, 354–363. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/nph.13592&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d46614e904">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Michael, T. P. et al. Comprehensive definition of genome features in Spirodela polyrhiza by high-depth physical mapping and short-read DNA sequencing strategies. Plant J. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.13400&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d46614e907">25</a></sup> were used as references to order contigs as described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Darling, A. C., Mau, B., Blattner, F. R. &amp; Perna, N. T. Mauve: multiple alignment of conserved genomic sequence with rearrangements. Genome Res. 14, 1394–1403. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1101/gr.2289704&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2004)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d46614e911">33</a></sup>. The resulting scaffolds (N50 = 1,7 Mbp) were super-scaffolded by SSPACE-Longread v.1–1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Boetzer, M. &amp; Pirovano, W. SSPACE-LongRead: scaffolding bacterial draft genomes using long read sequence information. BMC Bioinform. 15, 211. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1186/1471-2105-15-211&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2014)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d46614e915">34</a></sup> and assigned to the 18 chromosomes of <i>S. intermedia,</i> using 93 <i>S. polyrhiza</i> BACs as landmarks which were cross-hybridized to the <i>S. intermedia</i> chromosomes of clone 8410<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e929">29</a></sup>. In addition to confirmation of the same linkage relationship in clone 7747 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig1">1</a>), new cytogenetic probes using BACs from the genomic regions of interest were designed for FISH experiments to approve localization of the contigs within the pseudomolecules, to resolve mis-assemblies and/or to confirm new linkages (see below). Furthermore, contiguity of the assembly was confirmed by corrected ON reads of <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 8410 using minimap2 v2.16<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Li, H. Minimap2: pairwise alignment for nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics 34, 3094–3100. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/bty191&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d46614e940">35</a></sup> (see below).</p><p>After reiterative rounds of manual curation and validation by FISH, in the final genome assembly, 18 scaffolds (N50 = 8.3 Mbp) of in total 131.4 Mbp (82.2% of the estimated genome size) could be assigned to the 18 chromosomes (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Tab1">1</a>). Six of them show telomeric sequences at both ends and seven at least on one end (see Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig2">2</a>). Most of the shorter and/or repetitive sequences (16.2 Mbp, corresponding 10.1% of the estimated genome size) (N50 = 27.1 Kbp) could not yet be assigned and were considered as additional pseudomolecule “SiUn”.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 Assembly statistics of <i>S. intermedia</i> clones.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/tables/1"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Figure 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-2-desc" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p>Rearrangements between <i>S. polyrhiza</i> (n = 20) and <i>S. intermedia</i> (n = 18), confirmed for chromosomes of clones 8410 and 7747. Enframed: newly found rearrangement. Red boxes: present only in <i>S. polyrhiza</i>; green boxes: sequences present only in <i>S. intermedia.</i> Scale bar = 3 Mbp (based on PacBio assembly for clone 7747). Enumeration is as in Hoang &amp; Schubert (2017)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1383">29</a></sup> and in Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S3</a> (Short sequences present in S. p., but not chromosomally assigned in S. i. correspond to “SiUn” and are not considered). 13 ChrSi of the 7747 assembly show telomeric sequences at one (*) or both ends (**), while all pseudomolecules of the 8410 assembly show them at both ends.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Genome assembly for <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 8410 based on Illumina and Oxford Nanopore reads</h3><p>The ON/Illumina-derived scaffolds for clone 8410 were created using the MaSuRCA assembler and filtered using minimap2 to remove duplicated sequences derived from heterozygous regions. To form pseudomolecules, all 70 remaining scaffolds were corrected and ordered by manual curation using the assembly of clone 7747 as a reference. Finally, all 18 pseudomolecules ended at both sites with telomeric sequences. Merging of both assemblies revealed further small rearrangements between the karyotypes of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> and <i>S. intermedia</i> (see below and Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig2">2</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a>). The quality of both <i>S. intermedia</i> genome assemblies was assessed by the BUSCO program v. 3.1.0 <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Simao, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210–3212. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btv351&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1427">36</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Waterhouse, R. M. et al. BUSCO applications from quality assessments to gene prediction and phylogenomics. Mol. Biol. Evol. 35, 543–548. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/molbev/msx319&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1430">37</a></sup> with Embryophyta dataset 10 including 1375 genes (mostly from land plants). The hybrid assembly of ON/Illumina reads revealed 96.1% of the 1375 searched genes (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Tab1">1</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Figure 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-3-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="626" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>Circos plot of genomes of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> 9505 (orange) and <i>S. intermedia</i> 8410 (blue). (<b>A</b>) tracks representing the size of the pseudomolecules with a corresponding scale in 1 Mbp steps, with highlights every 5 Mbps, (<b>B</b>) total length of repeat features (in kbps) (<b>C</b>) gene density and (<b>D</b>) pairwise sequence synteny. The synteny link between gi|13 and Si02 is based on an error in the ON assembly for clone 9509 (see Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig5">5</a>). The region in question actually belongs to gi|2 as does the remaining part of Si02. Gene and repeat density are plotted in 0.5 Mbps bins. Data for <i>S. polyrhiza</i> 9505 are from Michael et al. 2017<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Michael, T. P. et al. Comprehensive definition of genome features in Spirodela polyrhiza by high-depth physical mapping and short-read DNA sequencing strategies. Plant J. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.13400&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1472">25</a></sup>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Gene prediction</h3><p>Based on similarity to nine aquatic and non-aquatic angiosperm reference genomes, including two duckweed species, <i>S. polyrhiza</i> 7498 v3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Michael, T. P. et al. Comprehensive definition of genome features in Spirodela polyrhiza by high-depth physical mapping and short-read DNA sequencing strategies. Plant J. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.13400&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1495">25</a></sup> and <i>Lemna minor</i> 5500<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Van Hoeck, A. et al. The first draft genome of the aquatic model plant Lemna minor opens the route for future stress physiology research and biotechnological applications. Biotech. Biofuels 8, 188. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1186/s13068-015-0381-1&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2015)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1502">38</a></sup>, gene model prediction via <u>Ge</u>ne <u>Mo</u>del <u>Ma</u>pper—GeMoMa<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Keilwagen, J. et al. Using intron position conservation for homology-based gene prediction. Nucl. Acids Res. 44, e89. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/nar/gkw092&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1516">39</a></sup> suggested in total 22,245 (Pacbio, clone 7747) or 21,594 (ON/Illumina, clone 8410) protein/RNA-coding genes, some more than predicted for <i>S. polyrhiza</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Michael, T. P. et al. Comprehensive definition of genome features in Spirodela polyrhiza by high-depth physical mapping and short-read DNA sequencing strategies. Plant J. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.13400&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1522">25</a></sup> (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S1</a>).</p><p>A total number of 16,162 genes of clone 7747, 16,493 of clone 8410 and 11,327 of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clone 9509 are coinciding with eggNOGs (Non-supervised Orthologous Groups). Comparing the proportion of eggNOG functional categories between the genomes of the two <i>Spirodela</i> species, the differences were &lt; 1%. Only the category ‘Energy production and conversion’, is overrepresented in <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747 (4.2 versus 3.1% in clone 8410 and 2.6% in <i>S. polyrhiza</i>) and the category ‘Replication, recombination and repair’ in clone 8410 (5.3% versus 3.2% in clone 7747 and 2.3% in <i>S. polyrhiza</i>) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S2</a>, Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S2</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">New linkages in <i>S. intermedia</i> as revealed by genome assembly and FISH</h3><p>The PacBio assembly for clone 7747 indicated a new rearrangement involving ChrSp20. This chromosome did not form the entire ChrSi18 as reported<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1567">29</a></sup>, instead it is split into two parts, the largest part corresponding to ChrSi18 and two rather small regions (between ChrSp20 3.72–3.78 and 3.80–3.96 Mbp) transferred to ChrSi16 (42,000–175,000 bp) (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S3</a>). Therefore, the previously not tested BAC 013O04 belonging ChrSp20 was selected for mcFISH experiments. The presence of this BAC sequence in <i>S. polyrhiza</i> ChrSp20 was confirmed by FISH (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig4">4</a>a). FISH results on <i>S. intermedia</i> chromosomes (clone 8410: Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig4">4</a>b, and clone 7747: Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig4">4</a>c) showed that BAC 013O04 (yellow) labeled the same chromosome (ChrSi16) as the BACs belonging to ChrSp15 (red), while the remaining part of ChrSp20 (green) labeled another chromosome pair (ChrSi18). This result confirmed that ChrSp20 became split and a very small part became translocated to ChrSp15, forming ChrSi16 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig2">2</a>), as inferred by PacBio assembly. Because only 76 kbp of the BAC 013O04 sequence appeared in the ON/Illumina assembly of ChrSi16, this link is not visible in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a> where the entire chromosome ChrSp20 is represented by the <i>S. intermedia</i> chromosome ChrSi18, based on the assembly results for clone 8410.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Figure 4"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 4</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig4_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-4-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig4_HTML.jpg" alt="figure4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="469" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p>New rearrangement between ChrSp 20 and ChrSp 15 in <i>S. intermedia</i> (<b>a</b>) The newly tested BAC 013O04 (yellow) belongs to ChrSp 20 (green) in <i>S. polyrhiza</i>; (<b>b</b>,<b>c</b>) BAC 013O04 was translocated to ChrSp 15 (red) forming ChrSi 16 in <i>S. intermedia</i> clones 8410 and 7747. Scale bars = 5 µm.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Furthermore, a piece of ChrSp13 (0.46–0.68 Mpbs), according to the ON assembly for ChrSp13 of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clone 9509, became integrated into ChrSi02 (5.43–5.66 Mbps) as suggested by the assemblies for both <i>S. intermedia</i> clones (for clone 8410 see Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a>). However, three BACs from this region (029A10, 028I16 and 037J09, together 649,507 bp) used as FISH probe, labeled ChrSp02 of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clones 7498 and 9509 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig5">5</a>) and appear on ChrSp02 also in the Bionano map (CP019095.1) of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clone 9509<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Michael, T. P. et al. Comprehensive definition of genome features in Spirodela polyrhiza by high-depth physical mapping and short-read DNA sequencing strategies. Plant J. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.13400&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1658">25</a></sup> as well as in pseudomolecule 1 (corresponding ChrSp02) of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clone 7498<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Cao, H. X. et al. The map-based genome sequence of Spirodela polyrhiza aligned with its chromosomes, a reference for karyotype evolution. New Phytol. 209, 354–363. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/nph.13592&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1665">23</a></sup> (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S4</a>). This uncovers a hitherto overlooked error in the ON assembly for <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clone 9509<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Hoang, P. N. T. et al. Generating a high-confidence reference genome map of the Greater Duckweed by integration of cytogenomic, optical mapping and Oxford Nanopore technologies. Plant J. 96, 670–684. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.14049&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1676">24</a></sup>. Another new small region, for which no BAC is available, became transferred from ChrSp14 (4.9–5.4 Mbps) to ChrSi04 (9.5–9.9 Mbps) and appeared in both assemblies (for clone 8410 see Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-5" data-title="Figure 5"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig5" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 5</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig5_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-5-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig5_HTML.jpg" alt="figure5" loading="lazy" width="685" height="420" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p>Evidence for ON mis-assembly of chromosome 13 of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> 9509. The newly tested BACs 029A10, 028I16 and 037J09 (yellow) belong to ChrSp 02 (red) of <i>S. polyrhiza</i> clone 9509 (upper panel) and clone 7498 (lower panel), not to ChrSp13. Scale bars = 5 µm.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Although only one BAC from ChrSp16 was tested previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1710">29</a></sup>, the assemblies from PacBio and ON reads suggests that the entire ChrSp16 is included in <i>S. intermedia</i> ChrSi11 together with a part of ChrSp10 (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig2">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">Types, abundance and distribution of repetitive elements</h3><p>Characterization of <i>S. intermedia</i> repetitive sequences was first performed by analyzing unassembled Illumina reads from the clone 8410 using the RepeatExplorer pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Novak, P., Neumann, P., Pech, J., Steinhaisl, J. &amp; Macas, J. RepeatExplorer: a Galaxy-based web server for genome-wide characterization of eukaryotic repetitive elements from next-generation sequence reads. Bioinformatics 29, 792–793. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btt054&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2013)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d46614e1734">40</a></sup>. This analysis served as a control for repeat quantification in the assembled pseudomolecules that may be biased due to the exclusion of satellite DNA or other repeats that are hard to assemble. In addition, the RepeatExplorer output was used to compile a reference database of <i>S. intermedia</i> repeats that was used to annotate the genome assemblies.</p><p>The RepeatExplorer analysis of 2.4 million paired-end Illumina reads (2.25 × genome coverage) revealed relatively small proportions of highly and moderately repeated sequences in the <i>S. intermedia</i> genome (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Tab2">2</a>). The repeats accounted for 20% of the genome, with LTR-retrotransposons representing the most abundant repeat class (14.1% of the genome, with Ty3/gypsy to Ty1/copia ratio of 2.17). Other repeats including LINEs, rDNA and satellite DNA made up only minor genome proportions.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table 2 Repeat proportions [%] estimated for unassembled sequence reads and genome assemblies of <i>S. intermedia</i> clones 8410 and 7747.</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/tables/2"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Repeat annotations of the genome assemblies using the RepeatExplorer reference database resulted in 18.5% and 20.2% of the 8410 and 7747 sequences marked as repetitive, respectively. These proportions correspond to the estimate obtained for unassembled reads (20.0%), suggesting that repeats were not significantly depleted in the final assemblies. Inspection of individual repeat categories revealed that partial depletion resulting in smaller proportions in the assembled genomes occurred for satellite repeats in both clones and for rDNA in the clone 7747 (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Tab2">2</a>). To obtain an alternative estimate of repeat proportions, we also analyzed both assemblies using RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; De Pevzner, P. A. novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21(Suppl 1), i351-358. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/bti1018&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2005)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2268">41</a></sup> that performs <i>de-novo</i> identification of repetitive elements based on the high frequency k-mers. This program estimated total repeat proportions of 23.1% (8410) and 25.6% (7747), most likely due to its better sensitivity for low-copy repeats (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Tab2">2</a>).</p><p>An interesting observation was the relatively high abundance of simple-sequence repeats, especially the microsatellite motif (AG)<sub>n</sub>, that was revealed by Tandem Repeats Finder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucl. Acids Res. 27, 573–580. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1093/nar/27.2.573&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (1999)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2283">42</a></sup> analysis within the assembled genomes and the Illumina reads. About 37,000 loci of (AG)<sub>n</sub> with an average length of 38 bp were detected in 8410, making up 1% of the assembly (the same proportion and characteristics were found for (AG)<sub>n</sub> in the 7747 assembly). These dispersed simple repeat loci appeared in the <i>S. intermedia</i> genome with an average frequency of one per 3.7 kb.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9">Characterization of rDNA loci</h3><p>Chromosome analysis of <i>S. intermedia</i> by FISH using 5S and (18S + 26S) rDNA probes, detected one major locus of 5S rDNA on ChrSi15 (corresponding to ChrSp13) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S3</a>a) and a major locus of 45S rDNA on ChrSi01 (corresponding to ChrSp01) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S3</a>b). The chromosome-scale assembly and ON reads for Si8410 confirmed the presence of a 5S rDNA locus on ChrSi15, and revealed an additional locus on ChrSi14. The extra-long ON reads showed that the locus on ChrSi15 contains a cluster of thirty-one 5S rDNA repeats, whereas the locus on ChrSi14 is composed of seven and 13 5S rDNA repeats interrupted by two 6 kb long repeats of another sequence (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig6">6</a>b). The chromosome assembly, based on PacBio sequences, showed similar arrangement of 5S rDNA in Si7747 with slightly different copy numbers in each of the loci. Quantitative PCR estimation of 5S rDNA copy number in Si7747 and Si8410 genomes supports this data with 57 ± 10 copies of 5S rRNA genes for Si8410 and, 70 ± 20 copies for Si7747. Sequence alignments suggested that the 5SrDNA units of the two loci contain slightly different non-transcribed spacers (NTS). This was confirmed by sequencing of the 5S rDNA repeats, amplified from genomic DNA of clones 8410 and 7747. Analysis of individual 5S rDNA clones of Si8410 and Si7747 identified the 119 bp long 5S rRNA genes with 100% identity to the previously sequenced 5S rRNA gene of <i>S. polyrhiza</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Borisjuk, N. et al. Structural and biochemical properties of duckweed surface cuticle. Front. Chem. 6, 317. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.3389/fchem.2018.00317&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2316">43</a></sup>, and two variants of the NTS for each ecotype (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#MOESM1">S4</a>), with variant 8410-1 corresponding to 5S rDNA locus on chromosome ChrSi15 and the variant 8410-2 corresponding to the locus on chromosome ChrSi14 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig6">6</a>a).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-6" data-title="Figure 6"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig6" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Figure 6</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/6" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig6_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-6-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41598-020-75728-9/MediaObjects/41598_2020_75728_Fig6_HTML.png" alt="figure6" loading="lazy" width="685" height="379" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-6-desc"><p>Schematic representation of rDNA loci in <i>S. intermedia</i> 8410. (<b>a</b>) Depiction of 45S rDNA loci at chromosomes ChrSi01 and ChrSi06; <b>Tel</b> = telomere. (<b>b</b>) Depiction of 5S rDNA loci at chromosome ChrSi15, and ChrSi14. The ChrSi15 locus contains 31 5S rDNA units with NTS of type-1; the ChrSi14 locus is composed of two clusters of 7 and 13 5S rDNA units of type-2 NTS, separated by a doubled 6 kb sequence of unknown function.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9/figures/6" data-track-dest="link:Figure6 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>In agreement with the FISH data, the genome assembly revealed a 45S rDNA locus in a distal position on ChrSi01 for both clones, Si7747 and Si8410. Extra-long ON reads confirmed this locus for Si8410, about 83 kb upstream of one ChrSi01 chromosome telomere. Moreover, ON reads revealed an additional cluster of 45S rDNA repeats about 8 kb upstream the telomere on ChrSi06. Unlike the situation with 5S rDNA loci, there are no read-through sequences containing the whole 45S rDNA loci. Therefore, it is not possible to determine exactly how many of the 93 ± 25 45S rDNA copies estimated by qPCR for Si8410, are located in the minor locus.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec10" data-title="Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec10-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec10">Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec10-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Chromosome rearrangements between the two Spirodela species</h3><p>Previously, chromosome homeology and rearrangements between <i>S. polyrhiza</i> and <i>S. intermedia</i> were uncovered by comparative serial multicolor cross-hybridization to the <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 8410<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2382">29</a></sup>. Here, we applied the same approach, using informative BACs out of the 96 ones anchored in the <i>S. polyrhiza</i> genome, and found the same chromosomal rearrangements in <i>S. intermedia</i> clone 7747 as reported for clone 8410<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2393">29</a></sup>. Reiterative rounds of genome assembly and validation by FISH revealed a new linkage compared to the <i>S. polyrhiza</i> genome, in addition to the eight translocations detected previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2400">29</a></sup>. This new linkage involves ChrSi16, which received small parts from one end of ChrSp20 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig2">2</a>). A small piece, apparently transferred from one end of ChrSp13 to ChrSi02, turned out to be an error within the previous ON assembly for ChrSp13 of clone 9509<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Hoang, P. N. T. et al. Generating a high-confidence reference genome map of the Greater Duckweed by integration of cytogenomic, optical mapping and Oxford Nanopore technologies. Plant J. 96, 670–684. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1111/tpj.14049&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2018)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2407">24</a></sup>. Another small region, transferred from ChrSp14 to ChrSi04 was not studied by FISH, but it appeared in both assemblies. The <i>S. intermedia</i> chromosomes ChrSi03, 04, 06, 07, 09 and 11, previously found to be involved in evolutionary rearrangements, correspond in total to 10 <i>S. polyrhiza</i> chromosomes (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig1">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig2">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#Fig3">3</a> and<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2427">29</a></sup>). Now, at least two more rearrangements (in addition to the previously postulated one inversion and eight translocations) have to be assumed if the <i>S. polyrhiza</i> karyotype is more similar to that of the ancestor. Alternatively, eight (instead of six) translocations (involving ChrSi03, 04, 06, 07, 08, 11, 12, 16, 18), and one fission (ChrSi09)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Hoang, P. T. N. &amp; Schubert, I. Reconstruction of chromosome rearrangements between the two most ancestral duckweed species Spirodela polyrhiza and S. intermedia. Chromosoma 126, 729–739. &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s00412-017-0636-7&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2017)." href="/articles/s41598-020-75728-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d46614e2435">29</a></sup> were required if the <i>S. intermedia</i> karyotype is the more ancestral one. Additionally, we found a positional change of the smaller 5S rDNA locus to ChrSi14 (instead of ChrSi07 which harbors sequences adjacent to the minor 5S rDNA locus on ChrSp06).</p><p>The increased number of rearrangements refined our knowledge about karyotype evolution between <i>S. polyrhiza</i> and <i>S. intermedia</i> and made the corresponding genome assembly for both <i>S. intermedia</i> clones robust by independent confirmation.
